CHAPTER XII.	 12.911953956184709
Elizabeth awoke the next morning to the same thoughts and meditations	 18.007251534225862
which had at length closed her eyes. She could not yet recover from the	 18.975734640135965
surprise of what had happened; it was impossible to think of any thing	 17.853055154173543
else, and totally indisposed for employment, she resolved soon after	 72.69069177276974
breakfast to indulge herself in air and exercise. She was proceeding	 32.7047133278845
directly to her favourite walk, when the recollection of Mr. Darcy's	 26.81771621906183
sometimes coming there stopped her, and instead of entering the park,	 55.208322075242314
she turned up the lane, which led her farther from the turnpike road.	 35.44751888209443
The park paling was still the boundary on one side, and she soon passed	 38.06895669079011
one of the gates into the ground.	 25.657118312335037
After walking two or three times along that part of the lane, she was	 11.711608373280159
tempted, by the pleasantness of the morning, to stop at the gates and	 17.616998464025322
look into the park. The five weeks which she had now passed in Kent, had	 38.567525953994604
made a great difference in the country, and every day was adding to the	 16.036945008123332
verdure of the early trees. She was on the point of continuing her walk,	 21.456035982949363
when she caught a glimpse of a gentleman within the sort of grove which	 20.325778298664883
edged the park; he was moving that way; and fearful of its being Mr.	 37.91912550730183
Darcy, she was directly retreating. But the person who advanced, was now	 51.08988462643474
near enough to see her, and stepping forward with eagerness, pronounced	 32.37445323552186
her name. She had turned away, but on hearing herself called, though in	 43.817896854985065
a voice which proved it to be Mr. Darcy, she moved again towards the	 25.949479802743372
gate. He had by that time reached it also, and holding out a letter,	 92.9537015547593
which she instinctively took, said with a look of haughty composure, "I	 61.89748779114748
have been walking in the grove some time in the hope of meeting you.	 29.02938817717804
Will you do me the honour of reading that letter?"--And then, with a	 44.67385162056284
slight bow, turned again into the plantation, and was soon out of	 28.913874162584673
sight.	 4014.8117263307754
With no expectation of pleasure, but with the strongest curiosity,	 33.66263573766039
Elizabeth opened the letter, and to her still increasing wonder,	 45.89150379428898
perceived an envelope containing two sheets of letter paper, written	 108.35315233474975
quite through, in a very close hand.--The envelope itself was likewise	 63.494835595386256
full.--Pursuing her way along the lane, she then began it. It was dated	 32.26976068596029
from Rosings, at eight o'clock in the morning, and was as follows:--	 44.42260947889979
"Be not alarmed, Madam, on receiving this letter, by the	 54.1034229246798
apprehension of its containing any repetition of those sentiments,	 31.353484957331016
or renewal of those offers, which were last night so disgusting to	 18.633077364165754
you. I write without any intention of paining you, or humbling	 26.85367388676311
myself, by dwelling on wishes, which, for the happiness of both,	 50.58598449409637
cannot be too soon forgotten; and the effort which the formation,	 30.65301063217735
and the perusal of this letter must occasion, should have been	 29.239671640030544
spared, had not my character required it to be written and read.	 87.15905072676814
You must, therefore, pardon the freedom with which I demand your	 27.969646456749487
attention; your feelings, I know, will bestow it unwillingly, but I	 59.53820364993901
demand it of your justice.	 105.27616492279917
"Two offences of a very different nature, and by no means of equal	 33.96744588693905
magnitude, you last night laid to my charge. The first mentioned	 45.138870155527925
was, that, regardless of the sentiments of either, I had detached	 44.84409475842994
Mr. Bingley from your sister,--and the other, that I had, in	 50.233899993765625
defiance of various claims, in defiance of honour and humanity,	 27.508000593996453
ruined the immediate prosperity, and blasted the prospects of Mr.	 14.419671480345526
Wickham.--Wilfully and wantonly to have thrown off the companion of	 16.0273291239512
my youth, the acknowledged favourite of my father, a young man who	 43.59617081068217
had scarcely any other dependence than on our patronage, and who	 28.21997582941666
had been brought up to expect its exertion, would be a depravity,	 21.168687233219597
to which the separation of two young persons, whose affection could	 53.48296999266025
be the growth of only a few weeks, could bear no comparison.--But	 28.76038576462225
from the severity of that blame which was last night so liberally	 16.668708445861046
bestowed, respecting each circumstance, I shall hope to be in	 47.62577297285
future secured, when the following account of my actions and their	 50.376639559866014
motives has been read.--If, in the explanation of them which is	 42.23841747706813
due to myself, I am under the necessity of relating feelings which	 34.51059230950442
may be offensive to your's, I can only say that I am sorry.--The	 20.30116574275688
necessity must be obeyed--and farther apology would be absurd.--I	 47.473298993273346
had not been long in Hertfordshire, before I saw, in common with	 25.646341310786546
others, that Bingley preferred your eldest sister, to any other	 64.50928187411681
young woman in the country.--But it was not till the evening of the	 23.34452527234518
dance at Netherfield that I had any apprehension of his feeling a	 39.3993952963522
serious attachment.--I had often seen him in love before.--At that	 43.22417523394515
ball, while I had the honour of dancing with you, I was first made	 51.41802699323312
acquainted, by Sir William Lucas's accidental information, that	 64.13672253497752
Bingley's attentions to your sister had given rise to a general	 73.07313489770304
expectation of their marriage. He spoke of it as a certain event,	 32.611241149153464
of which the time alone could be undecided. From that moment I	 43.8477833117847
observed my friend's behaviour attentively; and I could then	 109.09577654885655
perceive that his partiality for Miss Bennet was beyond what I had	 60.570289253710165
ever witnessed in him. Your sister I also watched.--Her look and	 68.85869808452688
manners were open, cheerful and engaging as ever, but without any	 52.80937949495072
symptom of peculiar regard, and I remained convinced from the	 28.902599990927826
evening's scrutiny, that though she received his attentions with	 73.97909753108253
pleasure, she did not invite them by any participation of	 19.62545728184675
sentiment.--If _you_ have not been mistaken here, _I_ must have	 31.958437175238718
been in an error. Your superior knowledge of your sister must make	 49.131136997536316
the latter probable.--If it be so, if I have been misled by such	 34.55307369480706
error, to inflict pain on her, your resentment has not been	 81.86211214368612
unreasonable. But I shall not scruple to assert, that the serenity	 22.521917556952758
of your sister's countenance and air was such, as might have given	 39.681909048407796
the most acute observer, a conviction that, however amiable her	 51.680849706493866
temper, her heart was not likely to be easily touched.--That I was	 32.18761145411712
desirous of believing her indifferent is certain,--but I will	 54.409907256306916
venture to say that my investigations and decisions are not usually	 35.92685115830875
influenced by my hopes or fears.--I did not believe her to be	 17.860250640685702
indifferent because I wished it;--I believed it on impartial	 110.84556450337995
conviction, as truly as I wished it in reason.--My objections to	 71.45591743395977
the marriage were not merely those, which I last night acknowledged	 63.023703779822554
to have required the utmost force of passion to put aside, in my	 33.912281482989776
own case; the want of connection could not be so great an evil to	 31.438659853757212
my friend as to me.--But there were other causes of	 43.48252732019997
repugnance;--causes which, though still existing, and existing to	 25.791254715167774
an equal degree in both instances, I had myself endeavoured to	 56.80490800969188
forget, because they were not immediately before me.--These causes	 39.002763573952855
must be stated, though briefly.--The situation of your mother's	 35.44331301012242
family, though objectionable, was nothing in comparison of that	 30.713650176890443
total want of propriety so frequently, so almost uniformly betrayed	 60.96555458373504
by herself, by your three younger sisters, and occasionally even by	 60.7064785877238
your father.--Pardon me.--It pains me to offend you. But amidst	 22.87278621816199
your concern for the defects of your nearest relations, and your	 30.437001752304027
displeasure at this representation of them, let it give you	 52.90818193663787
consolation to consider that, to have conducted yourselves so as to	 46.98129012232833
avoid any share of the like censure, is praise no less generally	 83.46259102883594
bestowed on you and your eldest sister, than it is honourable to	 28.0444021981084
the sense and disposition of both.--I will only say farther, that	 64.81825135913482
from what passed that evening, my opinion of all parties was	 54.79305414237041
confirmed, and every inducement heightened, which could have led me	 30.987666138602293
before, to preserve my friend from what I esteemed a most unhappy	 42.369459542512566
connection.--He left Netherfield for London, on the day following,	 34.48057618692267
as you, I am certain, remember, with the design of soon	 47.65404731489727
returning.--The part which I acted, is now to be explained.--His	 39.39188125586638
sisters' uneasiness had been equally excited with my own; our	 54.27380126893344
coincidence of feeling was soon discovered; and, alike sensible	 37.36971289627059
that no time was to be lost in detaching their brother, we shortly	 51.13201854310663
resolved on joining him directly in London.--We accordingly	 39.55723457707192
went--and there I readily engaged in the office of pointing out to	 41.32072527846074
my friend, the certain evils of such a choice.--I described, and	 29.47184468569696
enforced them earnestly.--But, however this remonstrance might have	 50.49523543922827
staggered or delayed his determination, I do not suppose that it	 14.693003721711083
would ultimately have prevented the marriage, had it not been	 62.41913254255917
seconded by the assurance which I hesitated not in giving, of your	 31.63664251645752
sister's indifference. He had before believed her to return his	 47.10740978161136
affection with sincere, if not with equal regard.--But Bingley has	 93.38904201575413
great natural modesty, with a stronger dependence on my judgment	 50.56133491389648
than on his own.--To convince him, therefore, that he had deceived	 54.096464425077215
himself, was no very difficult point. To persuade him against	 76.43938352897659
returning into Hertfordshire, when that conviction had been given,	 40.898819913905484
was scarcely the work of a moment.--I cannot blame myself for	 29.41774457593316
having done thus much. There is but one part of my conduct in the	 35.592412730916216
whole affair, on which I do not reflect with satisfaction; it is	 28.699473947960783
that I condescended to adopt the measures of art so far as to	 14.103110318868248
conceal from him your sister's being in town. I knew it myself, as	 40.34477306414261
it was known to Miss Bingley, but her brother is even yet ignorant	 52.38271485909207
of it.--That they might have met without ill consequence, is	 87.70435407135696
perhaps probable;--but his regard did not appear to me enough	 33.28446527885393
extinguished for him to see her without some danger.--Perhaps this	 31.632237822574115
concealment, this disguise, was beneath me.--It is done, however,	 38.228451595890455
and it was done for the best.--On this subject I have nothing more	 40.086876429345025
to say, no other apology to offer. If I have wounded your sister's	 28.64403708317709
feelings, it was unknowingly done; and though the motives which	 41.03246801182158
governed me may to you very naturally appear insufficient, I have	 36.05886380946145
not yet learnt to condemn them.--With respect to that other, more	 45.61808640571107
weighty accusation, of having injured Mr. Wickham, I can only	 40.74883969636243
refute it by laying before you the whole of his connection with my	 48.545642931746094
family. Of what he has _particularly_ accused me I am ignorant; but	 36.07654860409607
of the truth of what I shall relate, I can summon more than one	 27.811633551996856
witness of undoubted veracity. Mr. Wickham is the son of a very	 19.690073191487656
respectable man, who had for many years the management of all the	 34.61195997944298
Pemberley estates; and whose good conduct in the discharge of his	 18.51154280828614
trust, naturally inclined my father to be of service to him, and on	 65.80610385879449
George Wickham, who was his god-son, his kindness was therefore	 65.36091894846645
liberally bestowed. My father supported him at school, and	 42.054461311617075
afterwards at Cambridge;--most important assistance, as his own	 56.16477389110997
father, always poor from the extravagance of his wife, would have	 26.307403536983934
been unable to give him a gentleman's education. My father was not	 31.604124914883336
only fond of this young man's society, whose manners were always	 56.778181070762216
engaging; he had also the highest opinion of him, and hoping the	 24.402434254983177
church would be his profession, intended to provide for him in it.	 34.97142461668095
As for myself, it is many, many years since I first began to think	 28.96289319891043
of him in a very different manner. The vicious propensities--the	 16.360278897479844
want of principle which he was careful to guard from the knowledge	 30.379996249422547
of his best friend, could not escape the observation of a young man	 17.938052503749727
of nearly the same age with himself, and who had opportunities of	 48.02225979115112
seeing him in unguarded moments, which Mr. Darcy could not have.	 31.026944746696675
Here again I shall give you pain--to what degree you only can tell.	 37.55692552866756
But whatever may be the sentiments which Mr. Wickham has created, a	 26.48688619850343
suspicion of their nature shall not prevent me from unfolding his	 36.65030173711374
real character. It adds even another motive. My excellent father	 57.40528460534417
died about five years ago; and his attachment to Mr. Wickham was to	 17.618175952618717
the last so steady, that in his will he particularly recommended it	 76.05235056485516
to me, to promote his advancement in the best manner that his	 24.431821198959472
profession might allow, and if he took orders, desired that a	 67.06877041490671
valuable family living might be his as soon as soon as it became	 31.83277118263845
vacant. There was also a legacy of one thousand pounds. His own	 29.540857618795787
father did not long survive mine, and within half a year from these	 34.59962615857655
events, Mr. Wickham wrote to inform me that, having finally	 44.3326938691563
resolved against taking orders, he hoped I should not think it	 43.755592150597714
unreasonable for him to expect some more immediate pecuniary	 46.79841250041007
advantage, in lieu of the preferment, by which he could not be	 21.768910172060174
benefited. He had some intention, he added, of studying the law,	 48.78095864796376
and I must be aware that the interest of one thousand pounds would	 23.704999693728062
be a very insufficient support therein. I rather wished, than	 24.46987423261762
believed him to be sincere; but at any rate, was perfectly ready to	 39.93555126357179
accede to his proposal. I knew that Mr. Wickham ought not to be a	 23.3759874335251
clergyman. The business was therefore soon settled. He resigned all	 118.85089697061308
claim to assistance in the church, were it possible that he could	 34.74734755704626
ever be in a situation to receive it, and accepted in return three	 62.72285960167402
thousand pounds. All connection between us seemed now dissolved. I	 41.561654684360775
thought too ill of him, to invite him to Pemberley, or admit his	 35.61825069522646
society in town. In town I believe he chiefly lived, but his	 61.89386823246055
studying the law was a mere pretence, and being now free from all	 32.040664017648844
restraint, his life was a life of idleness and dissipation. For	 35.12677331309074
about three years I heard little of him; but on the decease of the	 32.25839672889523
incumbent of the living which had been designed for him, he applied	 18.75654378334349
to me again by letter for the presentation. His circumstances, he	 101.96270925169202
assured me, and I had no difficulty in believing it, were	 31.155551790877833
exceedingly bad. He had found the law a most unprofitable study,	 47.1111409592673
and was now absolutely resolved on being ordained, if I would	 32.15439778641813
present him to the living in question--of which he trusted there	 36.63596527488533
could be little doubt, as he was well assured that I had no other	 29.51537636625841
person to provide for, and I could not have forgotten my revered	 21.92510683895202
father's intentions. You will hardly blame me for refusing to	 24.04129279317899
comply with this entreaty, or for resisting every repetition of it.	 35.550340551459065
His resentment was in proportion to the distress of his	 25.100690390679205
circumstances--and he was doubtless as violent in his abuse of me	 34.8265578644283
to others, as in his reproaches to myself. After this period, every	 45.36617736342755
appearance of acquaintance was dropt. How he lived I know not. But	 60.980808606349804
last summer he was again most painfully obtruded on my notice. I	 31.16237818162344
must now mention a circumstance which I would wish to forget	 41.13287848055831
myself, and which no obligation less than the present should induce	 65.96593158067694
me to unfold to any human being. Having said thus much, I feel no	 47.74983363736612
doubt of your secrecy. My sister, who is more than ten years my	 40.847136407616894
junior, was left to the guardianship of my mother's nephew, Colonel	 13.262479962347982
Fitzwilliam, and myself. About a year ago, she was taken from	 69.75571478314644
school, and an establishment formed for her in London; and last	 34.31128485210887
summer she went with the lady who presided over it, to Ramsgate;	 46.21058955037697
and thither also went Mr. Wickham, undoubtedly by design; for there	 98.40216086358133
proved to have been a prior acquaintance between him and Mrs.	 23.162735881811702
Younge, in whose character we were most unhappily deceived; and by	 23.06506524912283
her connivance and aid, he so far recommended himself to Georgiana,	 39.1744356655532
whose affectionate heart retained a strong impression of his	 34.72036160803179
kindness to her as a child, that she was persuaded to believe	 37.880222534229944
herself in love, and to consent to an elopement. She was then but	 37.92027712457262
fifteen, which must be her excuse; and after stating her	 30.245880872143275
imprudence, I am happy to add, that I owed the knowledge of it to	 30.41938424713987
herself. I joined them unexpectedly a day or two before the	 39.587320241320434
intended elopement, and then Georgiana, unable to support the idea	 46.565907465536505
of grieving and offending a brother whom she almost looked up to as	 53.27899216749446
a father, acknowledged the whole to me. You may imagine what I felt	 46.38158699433292
and how I acted. Regard for my sister's credit and feelings	 51.50790142560907
prevented any public exposure, but I wrote to Mr. Wickham, who left	 52.192305591869335
the place immediately, and Mrs. Younge was of course removed from	 46.24378848175009
her charge. Mr. Wickham's chief object was unquestionably my	 36.6488202314334
sister's fortune, which is thirty thousand pounds; but I cannot	 27.948024298265477
help supposing that the hope of revenging himself on me, was a	 50.93020739430973
strong inducement. His revenge would have been complete indeed.	 29.278579198390066
This, madam, is a faithful narrative of every event in which we	 22.202627595019234
have been concerned together; and if you do not absolutely reject	 18.2295469957046
it as false, you will, I hope, acquit me henceforth of cruelty	 54.19571256109819
towards Mr. Wickham. I know not in what manner, under what form of	 46.78765110789821
falsehood he has imposed on you; but his success is not perhaps to	 36.733947291359094
be wondered at. Ignorant as you previously were of every thing	 49.521161376858416
concerning either, detection could not be in your power, and	 32.89519198721909
suspicion certainly not in your inclination. You may possibly	 37.77144854546718
wonder why all this was not told you last night. But I was not then	 36.854243481310256
master enough of myself to know what could or ought to be revealed.	 49.04806885222087
For the truth of every thing here related, I can appeal more	 25.229426418079658
particularly to the testimony of Colonel Fitzwilliam, who from our	 35.73161661238071
near relationship and constant intimacy, and still more as one of	 27.870576027112083
the executors of my father's will, has been unavoidably acquainted	 42.57545890014836
with every particular of these transactions. If your abhorrence of	 48.43939634159869
_me_ should make _my_ assertions valueless, you cannot be prevented	 37.79812481819438
by the same cause from confiding in my cousin; and that there may	 45.118845987485415
be the possibility of consulting him, I shall endeavour to find	 30.78359131252877
some opportunity of putting this letter in your hands in the course	 33.516459634521034
of the morning. I will only add, God bless you.	 29.59713998768131
"FITZWILLIAM DARCY."	 414.9209889585663
CHAPTER XIII.	 12.911953956184709
If Elizabeth, when Mr. Darcy gave her the letter, did not expect it to	 37.87135311835586
contain a renewal of his offers, she had formed no expectation at all of	 21.385618444179677
its contents. But such as they were, it may be well supposed how eagerly	 38.223447495310936
she went through them, and what a contrariety of emotion they excited.	 45.5669864567276
Her feelings as she read were scarcely to be defined. With amazement did	 48.82577909347207
she first understand that he believed any apology to be in his power;	 41.968875057988505
and steadfastly was she persuaded that he could have no explanation to	 19.002547773602146
give, which a just sense of shame would not conceal. With a strong	 76.35702796775048
prejudice against every thing he might say, she began his account of	 51.01359012748875
what had happened at Netherfield. She read, with an eagerness which	 18.035090698433475
hardly left her power of comprehension, and from impatience of knowing	 54.75755925429376
what the next sentence might bring, was incapable of attending to the	 44.826423278115605
sense of the one before her eyes. His belief of her sister's	 49.71634095172372
insensibility, she instantly resolved to be false, and his account of	 23.145080833737715
the real, the worst objections to the match, made her too angry to have	 40.86826265038327
any wish of doing him justice. He expressed no regret for what he had	 39.596444755858116
done which satisfied her; his style was not penitent, but haughty. It	 71.97832211556742
was all pride and insolence.	 37.913155794084744
But when this subject was succeeded by his account of Mr. Wickham, when	 21.727422425882146
she read with somewhat clearer attention, a relation of events, which,	 36.99490512365097
if true, must overthrow every cherished opinion of his worth, and which	 107.85442012243969
bore so alarming an affinity to his own history of himself, her feelings	 33.16719263832642
were yet more acutely painful and more difficult of definition.	 32.778578206860985
Astonishment, apprehension, and even horror, oppressed her. She wished	 62.090968957906654
to discredit it entirely, repeatedly exclaiming, "This must be false!	 26.915278108221816
This cannot be! This must be the grossest falsehood!"--and when she had	 27.115219827165866
gone through the whole letter, though scarcely knowing any thing of the	 14.751436532784599
last page or two, put it hastily away, protesting that she would not	 38.82235121061387
regard it, that she would never look in it again.	 41.340143071024514
In this perturbed state of mind, with thoughts that could rest on	 49.82075214684306
nothing, she walked on; but it would not do; in half a minute the letter	 41.41846344136603
was unfolded again, and collecting herself as well as she could, she	 17.990119659330627
again began the mortifying perusal of all that related to Wickham, and	 35.8425169481134
commanded herself so far as to examine the meaning of every sentence.	 15.203159536533317
The account of his connection with the Pemberley family, was exactly	 36.91595802265255
what he had related himself; and the kindness of the late Mr. Darcy,	 17.551919973638512
though she had not before known its extent, agreed equally well with his	 19.093663482880682
own words. So far each recital confirmed the other: but when she came to	 41.11224601041366
the will, the difference was great. What Wickham had said of the living	 137.59952724193707
was fresh in her memory, and as she recalled his very words, it was	 34.05134763851383
impossible not to feel that there was gross duplicity on one side or the	 26.94028611363371
other; and, for a few moments, she flattered herself that her wishes did	 32.38849630728391
not err. But when she read, and re-read with the closest attention, the	 26.48948423298983
particulars immediately following of Wickham's resigning all pretensions	 97.82548902062605
to the living, of his receiving in lieu, so considerable a sum as three	 44.36173546359211
thousand pounds, again was she forced to hesitate. She put down the	 44.48576522960563
letter, weighed every circumstance with what she meant to be	 45.56078676971292
impartiality--deliberated on the probability of each statement--but with	 33.2795198941407
little success. On both sides it was only assertion. Again she read on.	 48.73555644197483
But every line proved more clearly that the affair, which she had	 48.00880892786419
believed it impossible that any contrivance could so represent, as to	 48.14677856959208
render Mr. Darcy's conduct in it less than infamous, was capable of a	 29.84861858198026
turn which must make him entirely blameless throughout the whole.	 30.959047434159523
The extravagance and general profligacy which he scrupled not to lay to	 20.791950802010227
Mr. Wickham's charge, exceedingly shocked her; the more so, as she could	 54.88850777161987
bring no proof of its injustice. She had never heard of him before his	 27.02077886252614
entrance into the ----shire Militia, in which he had engaged at the	 32.282515634371336
persuasion of the young man, who, on meeting him accidentally in town,	 37.11086292458553
had there renewed a slight acquaintance. Of his former way of life,	 54.54553261000594
nothing had been known in Hertfordshire but what he told himself. As to	 36.088499226924874
his real character, had information been in her power, she had never	 27.138335750217184
felt a wish of enquiring. His countenance, voice, and manner, had	 56.130594525871714
established him at once in the possession of every virtue. She tried to	 29.39844061261977
recollect some instance of goodness, some distinguished trait of	 46.31219540243999
integrity or benevolence, that might rescue him from the attacks of Mr.	 17.01074780485013
Darcy; or at least, by the predominance of virtue, atone for those	 70.46747681854035
casual errors, under which she would endeavour to class, what Mr. Darcy	 27.112449557520534
had described as the idleness and vice of many years continuance. But no	 35.95630313730931
such recollection befriended her. She could see him instantly before	 53.87297348822818
her, in every charm of air and address; but she could remember no more	 37.94065195809103
substantial good than the general approbation of the neighbourhood, and	 38.61412860819743
the regard which his social powers had gained him in the mess. After	 28.8462377682196
pausing on this point a considerable while, she once more continued to	 40.14215715153598
read. But, alas! the story which followed of his designs on Miss Darcy,	 53.787329988357975
received some confirmation from what had passed between Colonel	 31.099060545606758
Fitzwilliam and herself only the morning before; and at last she was	 56.284272540604526
referred for the truth of every particular to Colonel Fitzwilliam	 28.817127664815033
himself--from whom she had previously received the information of his	 20.843299480865262
near concern in all his cousin's affairs, and whose character she had no	 24.44757540255931
reason to question. At one time she had almost resolved on applying to	 36.05847013267373
him, but the idea was checked by the awkwardness of the application, and	 16.833075270135698
at length wholly banished by the conviction that Mr. Darcy would never	 16.658757365385608
have hazarded such a proposal, if he had not been well assured of his	 22.37025534308674
cousin's corroboration.	 121.34288640875192
She perfectly remembered every thing that had passed in conversation	 52.38546968061466
between Wickham and herself, in their first evening at Mr. Philips's.	 39.89859549000836
Many of his expressions were still fresh in her memory. She was _now_	 28.02277586684564
struck with the impropriety of such communications to a stranger, and	 26.67799605158036
wondered it had escaped her before. She saw the indelicacy of putting	 42.43517457120163
himself forward as he had done, and the inconsistency of his professions	 15.553478957426728
with his conduct. She remembered that he had boasted of having no fear	 37.42017032988815
of seeing Mr. Darcy--that Mr. Darcy might leave the country, but that	 48.54660206646304
_he_ should stand his ground; yet he had avoided the Netherfield ball	 43.295212661455075
the very next week. She remembered also, that till the Netherfield	 52.751979339650774
family had quitted the country, he had told his story to no one but	 42.71123486471285
herself; but that after their removal, it had been every where	 75.16102153593188
discussed; that he had then no reserves, no scruples in sinking Mr.	 31.41045514855233
Darcy's character, though he had assured her that respect for the	 30.472952430264204
father, would always prevent his exposing the son.	 52.04713360222243
How differently did every thing now appear in which he was concerned!	 34.5145145398293
His attentions to Miss King were now the consequence of views solely and	 28.11848978199796
hatefully mercenary; and the mediocrity of her fortune proved no longer	 21.551789759859503
the moderation of his wishes, but his eagerness to grasp at any thing.	 26.404266266378468
His behaviour to herself could now have had no tolerable motive; he had	 30.41822350971071
either been deceived with regard to her fortune, or had been gratifying	 80.37720908471886
his vanity by encouraging the preference which she believed she had most	 55.72152568260307
incautiously shewn. Every lingering struggle in his favour grew fainter	 25.819743525134815
and fainter; and in farther justification of Mr. Darcy, she could not	 17.123225570053123
but allow that Mr. Bingley, when questioned by Jane, had long ago	 35.00777149498903
asserted his blamelessness in the affair; that proud and repulsive as	 24.55807206832529
were his manners, she had never, in the whole course of their	 27.068334407359554
acquaintance, an acquaintance which had latterly brought them much	 60.78210152303636
together, and given her a sort of intimacy with his ways, seen any thing	 35.78506643874307
that betrayed him to be unprincipled or unjust--any thing that spoke him	 38.797749927045444

esteemed and valued--that even Wickham had allowed him merit as a	 50.037982924593734
brother, and that she had often heard him speak so affectionately of	 30.7846690364431

his actions been what Wickham represented them, so gross a violation of	 38.72701627415661
every thing right could hardly have been concealed from the world; and	 27.30827082778447

She grew absolutely ashamed of herself.--Of neither Darcy nor Wickham	 52.06597683680872
could she think, without feeling that she had been blind, partial,	 16.22882783247684
prejudiced, absurd.	 10.85925182058365

often disdained the generous candour of my sister, and gratified my	 40.35377668865594

discovery!--Yet, how just a humiliation!--Had I been in love, I could	 45.46502022551725

From herself to Jane--from Jane to Bingley, her thoughts were in a line	 57.672843246729705
which soon brought to her recollection that Mr. Darcy's explanation	 60.296526143750185
_there_, had appeared very insufficient; and she read it again. Widely	 39.58458899445262
different was the effect of a second perusal.--How could she deny that	 32.267332847812185
credit to his assertions, in one instance, which she had been obliged to	 17.910847257563077
give in the other?--He declared himself to have been totally	 41.58508456693206

deny the justice of his description of Jane.--She felt that Jane's	 61.42264323906937
feelings, though fervent, were little displayed, and that there was a	 33.727476703764864
constant complacency in her air and manner, not often united with great	 31.7644479281466
sensibility.	 5545.038753112048

mentioned, in terms of such mortifying, yet merited reproach, her sense	 66.14141701544328

than on hers.	 74.37260059498585
The compliment to herself and her sister, was not unfelt. It soothed,	 22.751150541059886
but it could not console her for the contempt which had been thus	 25.090508763769964
self-attracted by the rest of her family;--and as she considered that	 14.461384888115823
Jane's disappointment had in fact been the work of her nearest	 38.39205860653632

had ever known before.	 38.066345540386536
After wandering along the lane for two hours, giving way to every	 50.17630735331331
variety of thought; re-considering events, determining probabilities,	 103.63681839896606
and reconciling herself as well as she could, to a change so sudden and	 26.679556693278023

reflections as must make her unfit for conversation.	 83.02873830267427
She was immediately told, that the two gentlemen from Rosings had each	 37.46859789125344
called during her absence; Mr. Darcy, only for a few minutes to take	 37.91832834803166
leave, but that Colonel Fitzwilliam had been sitting with them at least	 22.875995090785047

missing him; she really rejoiced at it. Colonel Fitzwilliam was no	 25.267124681819237
longer an object. She could think only of her letter.	 86.9113461562471
CHAPTER XIV.	 12.911953956184709
The two gentlemen left Rosings the next morning; and Mr. Collins having	 15.169441585473104
been in waiting near the lodges, to make them his parting obeisance, was	 33.25336364049778
able to bring home the pleasing intelligence, of their appearing in very	 42.265563506954734

melancholy scene so lately gone through at Rosings. To Rosings he then	 39.64743283242178

having them all to dine with her.	 69.08521686995287
Elizabeth could not see Lady Catherine without recollecting, that had	 30.50840078406357

CHAPTER XV.	 12.911953956184709
On Saturday morning Elizabeth and Mr. Collins met for breakfast a few	 47.17614174853767
minutes before the others appeared; and he took the opportunity of	 35.48090835072828

"I know not, Miss Elizabeth," said he, "whether Mrs. Collins has yet	 42.18358043404941

Jane looked well, and Elizabeth had little opportunity of studying her	 30.496169371768723
spirits, amidst the various engagements which the kindness of her aunt	 52.29387684665012
had reserved for them. But Jane was to go home with her, and at	 24.067586543576592
Longbourn there would be leisure enough for observation.	 41.549603957516375
It was not without an effort meanwhile that she could wait even for	 20.425325289221487
Longbourn, before she told her sister of Mr. Darcy's proposals. To know	 40.8348060700349
that she had the power of revealing what would so exceedingly astonish	 30.459765928526565
Jane, and must, at the same time, so highly gratify whatever of her own	 23.111204483392928
vanity she had not yet been able to reason away, was such a temptation	 24.04579932994122
to openness as nothing could have conquered, but the state of indecision	 38.7936758212676

and her fear, if she once entered on the subject, of being hurried into	 28.85862559994882
repeating something of Bingley, which might only grieve her sister	 59.60969950620405
farther.	 4694.658810476984
CHAPTER XVI.	 12.911953956184709
It was the second week in May, in which the three young ladies set out	 33.546630556523006
together from Gracechurch-street, for the town of ---- in Hertfordshire;	 62.822876393632534
and, as they drew near the appointed inn where Mr. Bennet's carriage was	 19.30648695182925
to meet them, they quickly perceived, in token of the coachman's	 25.04388223453068
punctuality, both Kitty and Lydia looking out of a dining-room up	 34.80648632003168
stairs. These two girls had been above an hour in the place, happily	 37.40406054532767
employed in visiting an opposite milliner, watching the sentinel on	 29.39819035555016
guard, and dressing a sallad and cucumber.	 29.603660781470396
After welcoming their sisters, they triumphantly displayed a table set	 99.97787796361047
out with such cold meat as an inn larder usually affords, exclaiming,	 33.43011600515847
"Is not this nice? is not this an agreeable surprise?"	 28.05322379100372

money, for we have just spent ours at the shop out there." Then shewing	 51.846521798159976

one wears this summer, after the ----shire have left Meryton, and they	 64.76354171218438

need not stay. Lydia laughed, and said,	 103.04644910148403

Elizabeth was shocked to think that, however incapable of such	 16.4425693886434
coarseness of _expression_ herself, the coarseness of the _sentiment_	 19.011136656263663

CHAPTER XVII.	 12.911953956184709
Elizabeth's impatience to acquaint Jane with what had happened could no	 41.13544257945563
longer be overcome; and at length resolving to suppress every particular	 32.526137788413415
in which her sister was concerned, and preparing her to be surprised,	 29.12393142404464
she related to her the next morning the chief of the scene between Mr.	 23.65642334957621
Darcy and herself.	 173.2825975409824

CHAPTER XVIII.	 12.911953956184709
The first week of their return was soon gone. The second began. It was	 34.92467638885236
the last of the regiment's stay in Meryton, and all the young ladies in	 22.453900978323226

Elizabeth was now to see Mr. Wickham for the last time. Having been	 30.257781306781837
frequently in company with him since her return, agitation was pretty	 71.97209326718914

"Nearly three weeks."	 314.7051280051521
"And you saw him frequently?"	 53.63553320871715

"His manners are very different from his cousin's."	 39.76157943516828

When the party broke up, Lydia returned with Mrs. Forster to Meryton,	 53.43680196825219

CHAPTER XIX.	 12.911953956184709
Had Elizabeth's opinion been all drawn from her own family, she could	 30.575579724575118
not have formed a very pleasing picture of conjugal felicity or domestic	 18.09531183704118
comfort. Her father captivated by youth and beauty, and that appearance	 83.3295558037679
of good humour, which youth and beauty generally give, had married a	 54.171178203859846
woman whose weak understanding and illiberal mind, had very early in	 89.38462069534638
their marriage put an end to all real affection for her. Respect,	 43.71707789530679
esteem, and confidence, had vanished for ever; and all his views of	 64.46921288076607
domestic happiness were overthrown. But Mr. Bennet was not of a	 42.726768554345696
disposition to seek comfort for the disappointment which his own	 52.721728791209046
imprudence had brought on, in any of those pleasures which too often	 72.74495378392955
console the unfortunate for their folly or their vice. He was fond of	 34.75277608853325
the country and of books; and from these tastes had arisen his principal	 45.14042159314768
enjoyments. To his wife he was very little otherwise indebted, than as	 34.13200859330175
her ignorance and folly had contributed to his amusement. This is not	 46.78221175860878
the sort of happiness which a man would in general wish to owe to his	 41.064725033254135
wife; but where other powers of entertainment are wanting, the true	 67.06115336560524
philosopher will derive benefit from such as are given.	 47.664424791341915
Elizabeth, however, had never been blind to the impropriety of her	 17.88314701695705
father's behaviour as a husband. She had always seen it with pain; but	 47.71722519101334
respecting his abilities, and grateful for his affectionate treatment of	 32.65399365982357
herself, she endeavoured to forget what she could not overlook, and to	 20.740575231914523
banish from her thoughts that continual breach of conjugal obligation	 21.885392877110995
and decorum which, in exposing his wife to the contempt of her own	 35.7939782212748
children, was so highly reprehensible. But she had never felt so	 42.52648305642717
strongly as now, the disadvantages which must attend the children of so	 66.96728131854987
unsuitable a marriage, nor ever been so fully aware of the evils	 29.542826225627806
arising from so ill-judged a direction of talents; talents which rightly	 22.891539432370887
used, might at least have preserved the respectability of his daughters,	 68.76013097292797
even if incapable of enlarging the mind of his wife.	 33.591235976139785
When Elizabeth had rejoiced over Wickham's departure, she found little	 54.18451559506693
other cause for satisfaction in the loss of the regiment. Their parties	 36.82095273258396
abroad were less varied than before; and at home she had a mother and	 28.195251076952232
sister whose constant repinings at the dulness of every thing around	 18.342256588978554
them, threw a real gloom over their domestic circle; and, though Kitty	 53.775251032506944
might in time regain her natural degree of sense, since the disturbers	 82.37892460436146
of her brain were removed, her other sister, from whose disposition	 64.65066206709156
greater evil might be apprehended, was likely to be hardened in all her	 23.38682608314904
folly and assurance, by a situation of such double danger as a watering	 43.69938939071025
place and a camp. Upon the whole, therefore, she found, what has been	 60.93384483638768
sometimes found before, that an event to which she had looked forward	 47.98807991285784
with impatient desire, did not in taking place, bring all the	 40.390949610323844
satisfaction she had promised herself. It was consequently necessary to	 27.76318895460035
name some other period for the commencement of actual felicity; to have	 20.427657716497492
some other point on which her wishes and hopes might be fixed, and by	 33.66265203460114
again enjoying the pleasure of anticipation, console herself for the	 50.12707007577681
present, and prepare for another disappointment. Her tour to the Lakes	 71.18367421420764
was now the object of her happiest thoughts; it was her best consolation	 29.64008248873034
for all the uncomfortable hours, which the discontentedness of her	 19.616576642420796

the scheme, every part of it would have been perfect.	 29.607363769849808
"But it is fortunate," thought she, "that I have something to wish for.	 37.22224779517746
Were the whole arrangement complete, my disappointment would be certain.	 46.09594080046066
But here, by carrying with me one ceaseless source of regret in my	 61.67984903286847
sister's absence, I may reasonably hope to have all my expectations of	 44.92054181524721
pleasure realized. A scheme of which every part promises delight, can	 128.8521164157684
never be successful; and general disappointment is only warded off by	 53.52929877874689

When Lydia went away, she promised to write very often and very minutely	 38.45538365066943
to her mother and Kitty; but her letters were always long expected, and	 28.503131365319934

The time fixed for the beginning of their Northern tour was now fast	 28.48130126986867

Elizabeth was excessively disappointed; she had set her heart on seeing	 27.45003704620557

was her business to be satisfied--and certainly her temper to be happy;	 71.25186609086805

With the mention of Derbyshire, there were many ideas connected. It was	 32.183796191566785
impossible for her to see the word without thinking of Pemberley and its	 32.34919999519801
owner. "But surely," said she, "I may enter his county with impunity,	 28.220847341086117

The period of expectation was now doubled. Four weeks were to pass away	 31.771109684060555
before her uncle and aunt's arrival. But they did pass away, and Mr. and	 46.75067879765191
Mrs. Gardiner, with their four children, did at length appear at	 52.104946170302725

Jane, who was the general favourite, and whose steady sense and	 30.11190258649415

The Gardiners staid only one night at Longbourn, and set off the next	 18.430387084845798

Lambton, Elizabeth found from her aunt, that Pemberley was situated. It	 61.40391675430184
was not in their direct road, nor more than a mile or two out of it. In	 25.194011644925638
talking over their route the evening before, Mrs. Gardiner expressed an	 55.68420433349738
inclination to see the place again. Mr. Gardiner declared his	 46.32835688635732
willingness, and Elizabeth was applied to for her approbation.	 24.70743120733326
"My love, should not you like to see a place of which you have heard so	 42.843753405551126
much?" said her aunt. "A place too, with which so many of your	 90.63280810253995
acquaintance are connected. Wickham passed all his youth there, you	 250.7881509862013
know."	 1152.1181923999723
Elizabeth was distressed. She felt that she had no business at	 23.551710447470633
Pemberley, and was obliged to assume a disinclination for seeing it. She	 43.1932002989495
must own that she was tired of great houses; after going over so many,	 61.2449467558247
she really had no pleasure in fine carpets or satin curtains.	 34.72461057531124
Mrs. Gardiner abused her stupidity. "If it were merely a fine house	 44.21337377312863
richly furnished," said she, "I should not care about it myself; but the	 17.560788711176027
grounds are delightful. They have some of the finest woods in the	 28.157039668865288
country."	 2014.0340064845823
Elizabeth said no more--but her mind could not acquiesce. The	 25.205752658917437
possibility of meeting Mr. Darcy, while viewing the place, instantly	 61.63391615280372
occurred. It would be dreadful! She blushed at the very idea; and	 50.22522860127805
thought it would be better to speak openly to her aunt, than to run	 28.95794144171864
such a risk. But against this, there were objections; and she finally	 65.55174158007543
resolved that it could be the last resource, if her private enquiries as	 49.211191005594266
to the absence of the family, were unfavourably answered.	 27.61467424905275
Accordingly, when she retired at night, she asked the chambermaid	 23.77709165809872
whether Pemberley were not a very fine place, what was the name of its	 51.64375276886024
proprietor, and with no little alarm, whether the family were down for	 45.280595248904774
the summer. A most welcome negative followed the last question--and her	 52.01700587770045
alarms being now removed, she was at leisure to feel a great deal of	 23.75011030969448
curiosity to see the house herself; and when the subject was revived the	 34.1740980201408
next morning, and she was again applied to, could readily answer, and	 31.518587270091196
with a proper air of indifference, that she had not really any dislike	 22.42914586989385
to the scheme.	 58.84422053120421
To Pemberley, therefore, they were to go.	 34.25492896317115

PRIDE & PREJUDICE.	 34.24156922046106
CHAPTER I.	 254.0372352719546
Elizabeth, as they drove along, watched for the first appearance of	 12.69899890965739
Pemberley Woods with some perturbation; and when at length they turned	 31.443006955952125
in at the lodge, her spirits were in a high flutter.	 53.87130710020665
The park was very large, and contained great variety of ground. They	 25.26207611516458
entered it in one of its lowest points, and drove for some time through	 32.52556486176615
a beautiful wood, stretching over a wide extent.	 42.85546388787944
Elizabeth's mind was too full for conversation, but she saw and admired	 61.81313734313146
every remarkable spot and point of view. They gradually ascended for	 42.80293799975982
half a mile, and then found themselves at the top of a considerable	 28.796687760493498
eminence, where the wood ceased, and the eye was instantly caught by	 22.703070573389002
Pemberley House, situated on the opposite side of a valley, into which	 22.587919205280095
the road with some abruptness wound. It was a large, handsome, stone	 25.011546701421196
building, standing well on rising ground, and backed by a ridge of high	 42.05262546920781
woody hills;--and in front, a stream of some natural importance was	 27.063747681782427
swelled into greater, but without any artificial appearance. Its banks	 98.23168442040364
were neither formal, nor falsely adorned. Elizabeth was delighted. She	 45.72801223464879
had never seen a place for which nature had done more, or where natural	 42.00590076985846
beauty had been so little counteracted by an awkward taste. They were	 30.65051913698074
all of them warm in their admiration; and at that moment she felt, that	 26.365780061933542
to be mistress of Pemberley might be something!	 41.61945894972413
They descended the hill, crossed the bridge, and drove to the door; and,	 21.429732009241953
while examining the nearer aspect of the house, all her apprehensions of	 24.543539754424486
meeting its owner returned. She dreaded lest the chambermaid had been	 79.35013472686036
mistaken. On applying to see the place, they were admitted into the	 32.797355924396705
hall; and Elizabeth, as they waited for the housekeeper, had leisure to	 46.47010196118504
wonder at her being where she was.	 30.35012263035095
The housekeeper came; a respectable-looking, elderly woman, much less	 46.68374366303167
fine, and more civil, than she had any notion of finding her. They	 30.84851144186288
followed her into the dining-parlour. It was a large, well-proportioned	 28.247522117564227
room, handsomely fitted up. Elizabeth, after slightly surveying it, went	 93.77192259672803
to a window to enjoy its prospect. The hill, crowned with wood, from	 43.049539466634926
which they had descended, receiving increased abruptness from the	 32.3407226481176
distance, was a beautiful object. Every disposition of the ground was	 66.39865710043128
good; and she looked on the whole scene, the river, the trees scattered	 38.52039423390931
on its banks, and the winding of the valley, as far as she could trace	 17.096420444646768
it, with delight. As they passed into other rooms, these objects were	 56.98655046392096
taking different positions; but from every window there were beauties to	 62.691641890433516
be seen. The rooms were lofty and handsome, and their furniture suitable	 67.34983091007344
to the fortune of their proprietor; but Elizabeth saw, with admiration	 33.06786479574371
of his taste, that it was neither gaudy nor uselessly fine; with less of	 57.862843911515775
splendor, and more real elegance, than the furniture of Rosings.	 21.79857748002151
"And of this place," thought she, "I might have been mistress! With	 45.508953811719635
these rooms I might now have been familiarly acquainted! Instead of	 23.962215263845426
viewing them as a stranger, I might have rejoiced in them as my own, and	 43.23067219089241
welcomed to them as visitors my uncle and aunt.--But no,"--recollecting	 52.06673986370348
herself,--"that could never be: my uncle and aunt would have been lost	 28.57435606801849
to me: I should not have been allowed to invite them."	 20.603140276000218
This was a lucky recollection--it saved her from something like regret.	 46.57453052614552
She longed to enquire of the housekeeper, whether her master were really	 42.771292191111456
absent, but had not courage for it. At length, however, the question was	 34.6855056156018
asked by her uncle; and she turned away with alarm, while Mrs. Reynolds	 32.17729442695253
replied, that he was, adding, "but we expect him to-morrow, with a	 33.67655958021277
large party of friends." How rejoiced was Elizabeth that their own	 126.52885397256921
journey had not by any circumstance been delayed a day!	 65.71342479232823
Her aunt now called her to look at a picture. She approached, and saw	 46.05216540085164
the likeness of Mr. Wickham suspended, amongst several other miniatures,	 19.896079187149585

The housekeeper came forward, and told them it was the picture of a	 27.559771525327672
young gentleman, the son of her late master's steward, who had been	 25.532911338155298
brought up by him at his own expence.--"He is now gone into the army,"	 33.30645300309891

Mrs. Gardiner looked at her niece with a smile, but Elizabeth could not	 12.880718244059185

"I have heard much of your master's fine person," said Mrs. Gardiner,	 20.293178472236036

"And do not you think him a very handsome gentleman, Ma'am?"	 19.00028082991293
"Yes, very handsome."	 371.90290525267756

"His father was an excellent man," said Mrs. Gardiner.	 33.87198932539582

The picture gallery, and two or three of the principal bed-rooms, were	 26.04765467660549

Darcy's, in crayons, whose subjects were usually more interesting, and	 35.488875121760955
also more intelligible.	 122.97744277522231

CHAPTER II.	 12.911953956184709
Elizabeth had settled it that Mr. Darcy would bring his sister to visit	 28.168131716142884
her, the very day after her reaching Pemberley; and was consequently	 41.54823128668493
resolved not to be out of sight of the inn the whole of that morning.	 35.2563025247519
But her conclusion was false; for on the very morning after their own	 40.9288575171454
arrival at Lambton, these visitors came. They had been walking about the	 34.72734077518431
place with some of their new friends, and were just returned to the inn	 22.22860471746006

livery, guessed what it meant, and imparted no small degree of surprise	 54.72031578060694
to her relations, by acquainting them with the honour which she	 36.383432070913244
expected. Her uncle and aunt were all amazement; and the embarrassment	 37.783205881283024

the business. Nothing had ever suggested it before, but they now felt	 80.7176262370432

newly-born notions were passing in their heads, the perturbation of	 15.793570208928058

at her own discomposure; but amongst other causes of disquiet, she	 41.293024114041444
dreaded lest the partiality of the brother should have said too much in	 37.40967398277308

She retreated from the window, fearful of being seen; and as she walked	 25.813548297315847
up and down the room, endeavouring to compose herself, saw such looks	 35.55657982088775

into somewhat of a friendlier nature, by the testimony so highly in his	 38.26971756661238
favour, and bringing forward his disposition in so amiable a light,	 74.43320142990291

overlooked. It was gratitude.--Gratitude, not merely for having once	 28.271018123922346
loved her, but for loving her still well enough, to forgive all the	 99.08649625144908

unjust accusations accompanying her rejection. He who, she had been	 32.49419388326786

their two selves only were concerned, was soliciting the good opinion	 76.83889014081012

esteemed, she was grateful to him, she felt a real interest in his	 33.24304905849916
welfare; and she only wanted to know how far she wished that welfare to	 27.196093303211686
depend upon herself, and how far it would be for the happiness of both	 32.6468004458442

possessed, of bringing on the renewal of his addresses.	 22.487278365387766
It had been settled in the evening, between the aunt and niece, that	 28.319317483831604
such a striking civility as Miss Darcy's, in coming to them on the very	 42.885416634794375
day of her arrival at Pemberley, for she had reached it only to a late	 41.41704042679609
breakfast, ought to be imitated, though it could not be equalled, by	 19.15612003239873
some exertion of politeness on their side; and, consequently, that it	 31.085444040941862
would be highly expedient to wait on her at Pemberley the following	 29.124014805261847
morning. They were, therefore, to go.--Elizabeth was pleased, though,	 71.09700618568773
when she asked herself the reason, she had very little to say in reply.	 43.353846855866934
Mr. Gardiner left them soon after breakfast. The fishing scheme had been	 27.766230808974807
renewed the day before, and a positive engagement made of his meeting	 62.60118103592047
some of the gentlemen at Pemberley by noon.	 36.192481845608334
CHAPTER III.	 12.911953956184709
Convinced as Elizabeth now was that Miss Bingley's dislike of her had	 81.08429280672061
originated in jealousy, she could not help feeling how very unwelcome	 11.791570539274174
her appearance at Pemberley must be to her, and was curious to know with	 36.69488656843377
how much civility on that lady's side, the acquaintance would now be	 44.410176661667215
renewed.	 4957.375175091107
On reaching the house, they were shewn through the hall into the saloon,	 23.282799779958488
whose northern aspect rendered it delightful for summer. Its windows	 85.48228137743537
opening to the ground, admitted a most refreshing view of the high woody	 24.349665653606717
hills behind the house, and of the beautiful oaks and Spanish chesnuts	 22.162707401884063
which were scattered over the intermediate lawn.	 27.32102716872811
In this room they were received by Miss Darcy, who was sitting there	 32.06239719410805
with Mrs. Hurst and Miss Bingley, and the lady with whom she lived in	 22.438736131694252
London. Georgiana's reception of them was very civil; but attended with	 59.52164163628122
all that embarrassment which, though proceeding from shyness and the	 44.22575169682381
fear of doing wrong, would easily give to those who felt themselves	 93.02693406570513
inferior, the belief of her being proud and reserved. Mrs. Gardiner and	 19.779457692647963
her niece, however, did her justice, and pitied her.	 41.49547574433199

short sentence, when there was least danger of its being heard.	 40.16625034160796

calling her attention. This observation would not have prevented her	 33.214242910079854

The next variation which their visit afforded was produced by the	 30.997939175371496
entrance of servants with cold meat, cake, and a variety of all the	 27.15891114659492
finest fruits in season; but this did not take place till after many a	 24.007654184894093

While thus engaged, Elizabeth had a fair opportunity of deciding whether	 74.0822505180364

He had been some time with Mr. Gardiner, who, with two or three other	 28.80900019865209
gentlemen from the house, was engaged by the river, and had left him	 40.65400949844027

CHAPTER IV.	 12.911953956184709
Elizabeth had been a good deal disappointed in not finding a letter from	 27.694649681749443

silence. At length, she spoke again. "I have just had a letter from	 38.86798264673235
Jane, with such dreadful news. It cannot be concealed from any one. My	 19.452718109134864
youngest sister has left all her friends--has eloped;--has thrown	 76.64965545558877
herself into the power of--of Mr. Wickham. They are gone off together	 45.595681671808265
from Brighton. _You_ know him too well to doubt the rest. She has no	 44.27024806969811
money, no connections, nothing that can tempt him to--she is lost for	 108.32082494300364
ever."	 753.6941685825765
Darcy was fixed in astonishment. "When I consider," she added, in a yet	 86.77935303505065
more agitated voice, "that _I_ might have prevented it!--_I_ who knew	 54.67261222656865
what he was. Had I but explained some part of it only--some part of what	 46.1708675074242
I learnt, to my own family! Had his character been known, this could not	 34.35136271194381
have happened. But it is all, all too late now."	 67.2038970696671
"I am grieved, indeed," cried Darcy; "grieved--shocked. But is it	 22.607811430803217
certain, absolutely certain?"	 100.81617578584778
"Oh yes!--They left Brighton together on Sunday night, and were traced	 40.50375339155191
almost to London, but not beyond; they are certainly not gone to	 98.89683081213508
Scotland."	 8598.018879251216
"And what has been done, what has been attempted, to recover her?"	 18.215338752760854
"My father is gone to London, and Jane has written to beg my uncle's	 42.84225358804751
immediate assistance, and we shall be off, I hope, in half an hour. But	 34.53778653633823
nothing can be done; I know very well that nothing can be done. How is	 29.969810148902106
such a man to be worked on? How are they even to be discovered? I have	 29.34604965068241
not the smallest hope. It is every way horrible!"	 139.32314332641423
Darcy shook his head in silent acquiesence.	 47.9522908305452
"When _my_ eyes were opened to his real character.--Oh! had I known what	 61.91637286034812
I ought, what I dared, to do! But I knew not--I was afraid of doing too	 62.06489163331576
much. Wretched, wretched, mistake!"	 27.850652348885536
Darcy made no answer. He seemed scarcely to hear her, and was walking up	 32.13270630769791
and down the room in earnest meditation; his brow contracted, his air	 35.15424970074542
gloomy. Elizabeth soon observed, and instantly understood it. Her power	 101.16781428723164
was sinking; every thing _must_ sink under such a proof of family	 35.19186864336486
weakness, such an assurance of the deepest disgrace. She could neither	 18.131590576023942
wonder nor condemn, but the belief of his self-conquest brought nothing	 41.93925837832281
consolatory to her bosom, afforded no palliation of her distress. It	 26.606552853467598
was, on the contrary, exactly calculated to make her understand her own	 22.241054431468438
wishes; and never had she so honestly felt that she could have loved	 47.93370252596002
him, as now, when all love must be vain.	 79.15613720968399
But self, though it would intrude, could not engross her. Lydia--the	 40.89884589137515
humiliation, the misery, she was bringing on them all, soon swallowed up	 52.14875754158264
every private care; and covering her face with her handkerchief,	 25.227849985802557
Elizabeth was soon lost to every thing else; and, after a pause of	 12.917873782860818
several minutes, was only recalled to a sense of her situation by the	 38.0126163616654
voice of her companion, who, in a manner, which though it spoke	 83.08741335552455
compassion, spoke likewise restraint, said, "I am afraid you have been	 37.517425158015996
long desiring my absence, nor have I any thing to plead in excuse of my	 57.24038654153842
stay, but real, though unavailing, concern. Would to heaven that any	 140.4359556948016
thing could be either said or done on my part, that might offer	 117.24566788087895
consolation to such distress.--But I will not torment you with vain	 37.397620809423195
wishes, which may seem purposely to ask for your thanks. This	 50.11317187088234
unfortunate affair will, I fear, prevent my sister's having the pleasure	 91.27851526219513
of seeing you at Pemberley to-day."	 28.382267766084702
"Oh, yes. Be so kind as to apologize for us to Miss Darcy. Say that	 24.723080442069524
urgent business calls us home immediately. Conceal the unhappy truth as	 70.88993483722659
long as it is possible.--I know it cannot be long."	 43.59421676513294
He readily assured her of his secrecy--again expressed his sorrow for	 27.96711210193057
her distress, wished it a happier conclusion than there was at present	 54.07591044549262
reason to hope, and leaving his compliments for her relations, with only	 61.687023835818714
one serious, parting, look, went away.	 49.67550059665075
As he quitted the room, Elizabeth felt how improbable it was that they	 24.400213284050825
should ever see each other again on such terms of cordiality as had	 56.0326621917177
marked their several meetings in Derbyshire; and as she threw a	 49.25350903354098
retrospective glance over the whole of their acquaintance, so full of	 36.324399163305884
contradictions and varieties, sighed at the perverseness of those	 15.191989669154472
feelings which would now have promoted its continuance, and would	 53.02862823246006
formerly have rejoiced in its termination.	 68.19374877299464
If gratitude and esteem are good foundations of affection, Elizabeth's	 89.44693223606144
change of sentiment will be neither improbable nor faulty. But if	 47.306984959610034
otherwise, if the regard springing from such sources is unreasonable or	 76.23419397414305
unnatural, in comparison of what is so often described as arising on a	 24.25110839912431
first interview with its object, and even before two words have been	 64.27787669663363
exchanged, nothing can be said in her defence, except that she had given	 33.031575590640166
somewhat of a trial to the latter method, in her partiality for Wickham,	 35.62096868844674
and that its ill-success might perhaps authorise her to seek the other	 40.895044790674106
less interesting mode of attachment. Be that as it may, she saw him go	 90.60729464326357
with regret; and in this early example of what Lydia's infamy must	 27.104866823041025
produce, found additional anguish as she reflected on that wretched	 39.77920251477585
business. Never, since reading Jane's second letter, had she entertained	 81.30291216272117
a hope of Wickham's meaning to marry her. No one but Jane, she thought,	 48.85053541183837
could flatter herself with such an expectation. Surprise was the least	 28.751992357492117
of her feelings on this developement. While the contents of the first	 16.214572867777655
letter remained on her mind, she was all surprise--all astonishment that	 65.00633872412824
Wickham should marry a girl, whom it was impossible he could marry for	 38.202363399602454
money; and how Lydia could ever have attached him, had appeared	 65.50695308332452
incomprehensible. But now it was all too natural. For such an attachment	 24.807807103452532
as this, she might have sufficient charms; and though she did not	 23.561300340602354
suppose Lydia to be deliberately engaging in an elopement, without the	 73.76420338508589
intention of marriage, she had no difficulty in believing that neither	 20.04484539034543
her virtue nor her understanding would preserve her from falling an easy	 44.45279503346614
prey.	 8.776652323334677
She had never perceived, while the regiment was in Hertfordshire, that	 36.86722244845377
Lydia had any partiality for him, but she was convinced that Lydia had	 18.253493272710944
wanted only encouragement to attach herself to any body. Sometimes one	 29.41729323473407
officer, sometimes another had been her favourite, as their attentions	 123.03570181247045
raised them in her opinion. Her affections had been continually	 50.77160179201671
fluctuating, but never without an object. The mischief of neglect and	 68.69669942587801
mistaken indulgence towards such a girl.--Oh! how acutely did she now	 79.3615356914072
feel it.	 76.17080270074008
She was wild to be at home--to hear, to see, to be upon the spot, to	 59.01689152136461
share with Jane in the cares that must now fall wholly upon her, in a	 57.276970648199054
family so deranged; a father absent, a mother incapable of exertion, and	 28.051157808513942
requiring constant attendance; and though almost persuaded that nothing	 27.48637943790114
could be done for Lydia, her uncle's interference seemed of the utmost	 55.14094641331095
importance, and till he entered the room, the misery of her impatience	 39.98426376972986
was severe. Mr. and Mrs. Gardiner had hurried back in alarm, supposing,	 49.390780947111935
by the servant's account, that their niece was taken suddenly ill;--but	 21.11310612934722
satisfying them instantly on that head, she eagerly communicated the	 27.373652135793677
cause of their summons, reading the two letters aloud, and dwelling on	 31.56776150624513
the postscript of the last, with trembling energy.--Though Lydia had	 24.86159897738074
never been a favourite with them, Mr. and Mrs. Gardiner could not but be	 29.502978143283368
deeply affected. Not Lydia only, but all were concerned in it; and after	 94.54404247079694
the first exclamations of surprise and horror, Mr. Gardiner readily	 22.159170975027916
promised every assistance in his power.--Elizabeth, though expecting no	 57.287420742657446
less, thanked him with tears of gratitude; and all three being actuated	 74.65122604263065
by one spirit, every thing relating to their journey was speedily	 37.29674381470696
settled. They were to be off as soon as possible. "But what is to be	 24.09321782482624
done about Pemberley?" cried Mrs. Gardiner. "John told us Mr. Darcy was	 69.84051096753794
here when you sent for us;--was it so?"	 75.0815113218349
"Yes; and I told him we should not be able to keep our engagement.	 23.351370651984478
_That_ is all settled."	 22.432470655002298
"That is all settled;" repeated the other, as she ran into her room to	 23.628408840648284
prepare. "And are they upon such terms as for her to disclose the real	 50.12501995756407
truth! Oh, that I knew how it was!"	 49.561507254493506
But wishes were vain; or at best could serve only to amuse her in the	 63.917702478436205
hurry and confusion of the following hour. Had Elizabeth been at leisure	 80.26384811204224
to be idle, she would have remained certain that all employment was	 33.949400095457044
impossible to one so wretched as herself; but she had her share of	 41.32880219851746
business as well as her aunt, and amongst the rest there were notes to	 29.266532872789327
be written to all their friends in Lambton, with false excuses for their	 58.94669598423023
sudden departure. An hour, however, saw the whole completed; and Mr.	 44.27383525649656
Gardiner meanwhile having settled his account at the inn, nothing	 129.47559994005468
remained to be done but to go; and Elizabeth, after all the misery of	 34.01753488155459
the morning, found herself, in a shorter space of time than she could	 19.848659284258403
have supposed, seated in the carriage, and on the road to Longbourn.	 60.6417049071233
CHAPTER V.	 12.911953956184709
"I have been thinking it over again, Elizabeth," said her uncle, as they	 37.105819944287724
drove from the town; "and really, upon serious consideration, I am much	 114.9540809962192
more inclined than I was to judge as your eldest sister does of the	 32.88703549011263
matter. It appears to me so very unlikely, that any young man should	 36.02101129381545
form such a design against a girl who is by no means unprotected or	 20.95614036813242
friendless, and who was actually staying in his colonel's family, that I	 31.082551081943176
am strongly inclined to hope the best. Could he expect that her friends	 41.24315661679479
would not step forward? Could he expect to be noticed again by the	 30.146352477319464
regiment, after such an affront to Colonel Forster? His temptation is	 45.142180050549506
not adequate to the risk."	 38.24266819602549
"Do you really think so?" cried Elizabeth, brightening up for a moment.	 33.036760043281326
"Upon my word," said Mrs. Gardiner, "I begin to be of your uncle's	 15.508823486607243
opinion. It is really too great a violation of decency, honour, and	 31.336791888438288
interest, for him to be guilty of it. I cannot think so very ill of	 18.462876208707137
Wickham. Can you, yourself, Lizzy, so wholly give him up, as to believe	 68.65952493739248
him capable of it?"	 26.783004163437354
"Not perhaps of neglecting his own interest. But of every other neglect	 32.49137464836782
I can believe him capable. If, indeed, it should be so! But I dare not	 42.73482346859598
hope it. Why should they not go on to Scotland, if that had been the	 57.51864376079953
case?"	 4015.9027181066112
"In the first place," replied Mr. Gardiner, "there is no absolute proof	 20.969949055549677
that they are not gone to Scotland."	 11.285642213607817
"Oh! but their removing from the chaise into an hackney coach is such a	 35.66960526936484
presumption! And, besides, no traces of them were to be found on the	 24.84796459986548
Barnet road."	 157.5791412278405
"Well, then--supposing them to be in London. They may be there, though	 43.76776420686238
for the purpose of concealment, for no more exceptionable purpose. It is	 25.79056444122778
not likely that money should be very abundant on either side; and it	 23.728195937972224
might strike them that they could be more economically, though less	 52.67324028380892
expeditiously, married in London, than in Scotland."	 164.2320872994167
"But why all this secrecy? Why any fear of detection? Why must their	 87.36723969856442

friend, you see by Jane's account, was persuaded of his never intending	 63.828964965985485
to marry her. Wickham will never marry a woman without some money. He	 41.34167508909886
cannot afford it. And what claims has Lydia, what attractions has she	 118.48969304564399
beyond youth, health, and good humour, that could make him for her sake,	 31.25547326815038
forego every chance of benefiting himself by marrying well? As to what	 36.685238887647664
restraint the apprehension of disgrace in the corps might throw on a	 45.18778371786906
